GAME: Blue Moon
RANK: 862
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Blue Moon seems to hit a sweet spot in my personal tastes: play after play, the game grows along with your proficiency with each deck, stretching the boundaries of a truly simple system and revealing unexpected and subtle complexities. As many others have already pointed out, it shares a good deal of Magic's charm (the different decks with distinctive gameplay and, of course, the deck building options, clearly to a much more limited extent) without the added weight of a CCG's first and often feared C. But, at least to me, the base game is already a great one: two decks of 30 cards, short playing time, well balanced and greatly themed, great replay value. Eventually, it's expandable, to the extent you prefer and without endangering its balance.

The oversized cards are really nice to see on the table, with the artwork ranging from good to great. The card quality could be much better, considering the lack of suitable card sleeves.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
After playing some other card games for a while, including casual play of Magic: The Gathering, I picked up the Buka Invasion deck because it was on sale and now I'm all excited to play Blue Moon again. This is a game that I never seem to get tired of. For a while I had downrated Blue Moon because it was less complex than CCGs, but now I see why Knizia elminated some CCG elements like land cards and matchups between individual creatures. The heart of a dueling card game is finding interesting card combos to whack your opponent with. Blue Moon lets you focus on that creativity without a lot of extra weight in the game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
After playing for several months, I feel I can now honestly rate it. My first play or two or three and I thought that the game was alright as I loved the card art and the little plastic dragons.  It's unfortunate that the board is poorly done and should have included an icon listing *with explanations* (I found a nice one on the bgeek and taped two copies onto the board). 

It was after 4 or 5 plays that I really started to feel the depth of the game's card play. In this game (like a lot of CCG's) "knowing your deck" (strengths and weaknesses) is very important. The game is more strategic than I first thought as I initially played it very tactically from hand to hand. But once all the possibilities started to unfold, I really began to enjoy the game. There's a luck factor that almost any card game has but a skilled player will know how to manage that as best as they can and can still come out a winner. 

I ended up buying about 4 more decks (Mimix, Terrah, Aqua, and Allies) after a few plays and I'm very glad for it. This is a game that I will go back to over the years with gaming joy.

RATING: 10
Even with just the base set, Blue Moon is a blast.  More than any other game in my collection, this game has approachability.  It's easy to learn, easy to teach, fairly short to play and very repeatable.  

The art on the cards is outstanding, the cards are big (tarot sized) and durable.  The theme really comes through, and the different decks have distinct personalities in game play, graphic design, and theme.

Blue Moon is one of my favorite 2 player games.  The fact that you can expand it with different decks definitely switches things up, and the deck building rules help with that as well.  It's one of my go-to games for gamers, kids, and non-gamers alike.

Problems occasionally loom (is it just a climbing game?  Are the decks really at all balanced?) but a bit more experience makes then suddenly vanish or transmute. RATING: 10
[Complete, with all people decks, both Emissaries & Inquisitors]

Rating not so much the core decks as the idea and rule system here -- the expansions definitely seem more fun, but this is more the "overall" rating of Blue Moon with a few expansions, in which case it's a quick, fun, not-pure-luck (there's plenty of strategy if you want it) but lots of excitement/luck card game.  

More importantly, we sure want to play this a lot, which is the best testament to it being pretty good.  A game that offers decent substance and high variability, in a short time frame, is going to get played many, many times, and generally make life better.  Blue Moon turns out to be that kind of game, perhaps more than any other we own.

UPDATE:  Down a hair.  Not that it's not great, I'm just slightly burned-out on the deck pairs that work well to play, and had a few sour games.  The Emissaries and Inquisitors additions are "meh."

UPDATE:  Back up, it's unreasonable to let Inquisitors take it down.

RATING: 5
Blue Moon has fantastic artwork, oversized cards that are easy to hold, and sturdy plastic dragons (very cool!) that are stored in a fitted Kosmos 2-player box. I find Blue Moon to be simple to learn and easy to play. I particularly like the game end trigger because it means that the games don't drag on: if one player gets all three dragons or the draw deck is exhausted, then all available cards are simply played out. I really appreciate the fact that the card decks are "pre-built" and non-collectible. The playing field is more balanced that way, since each deck is designed to be competitive. I used to play Magic: The Gathering, but it takes a lot of time and money for it to be worth it, especially if you play with people that are crazy for it. My friends had highly customized decks already, so I was at a bit of a disadvantage with my base deck and a few boosters.

UPDATE 1: The plastic dragon alone makes this one attractive, as well as the mechanic it brings. I waver on this one, but wavering towards the keep. UPDATE 2: Yeah, the plastic dragons and the card mat are really the only things I like - I'd rather play something else. The artwork is okay, the two races are uninspiring. My husband and sister are less than impressed. Like the classic card game War with slight variations.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
I'm still riding backlash against my middle school MtG addiction, and I'm a huge proponent of non-collectible card games as a result. I think people who like this game vastly overstate its "tactical complexity", but Blue Moon is still great as far as Magic-ish NCCGs go, and it's a work of art to boot. Nonetheless, I can't justify giving it a higher rating for two reasons:

1) It takes a number of games to "learn" how each deck plays and to get a good grasp on how the game works in general, so it's tough to bring non-gamers into the fold.

2) The base game is decidely stacked in favor of the Hoax once both players have a good grasp on how to play the game.

I'm on the fence about the expansions... I've seen the cards, thanks to the Blue Moon AI program, and they look really neat, but they'd be useless unless I can find somebody else to play with.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[i]Posted: 3/10/08, Rated: 8[/i]

I really enjoyed playing the collectible card game (CCG) [i][thing=463]Magic: The Gathering[/thing][/i] until I realized that in order to be truly competitive, I was going to have to spend a lot of money buying special cards.  I was resentful of that fact, and ultimately lost interest in playing it.  Although I haven't played a game in years, I still have fond memories of its highlights, chief among those being the process of building a deck.

The idea of a game which was CCG-like [i]without[/i] being a money pit like [i][thing=463]Magic: The Gathering[/thing][/i] was quite appealing.  I felt disoriented during my first few games of [i]Blue Moon:[/i] the game presents a different world, with its own unique mechanics.  Once I began to understand how it worked I realized that there was a beautfiully strategic battle to be fought.

There is no concept of "damaging" the other player's hit points.  Instead, you are trying to beat the other player's deck.  This is an important distinction, because losing a game doesn't feel as personal.  You can try for a fast win by overwhelming your opponent's ability to match your attack strength.  Alternatively, you can try to grind out a win over long rounds where more cards and special powers come into play.

The base game comes with two "races."  The "Vulca" are fiery creatures  who can quickly blaze to victory.  The "Hoax" are about deck control, and can neutralize that big offense.  These decks are not one-dimensional, as they actually have a few cards from other races as well.  This one matchup alone is excellent.

When you're ready for some more variety then there are expansions.  Unlike a true CCG, these expansions are also fixed-decks, which means you will get the same set of cards each time.  This is the feature which I love: I can spend a relatively small amount of money (the equivalent of two or three booster packs from a "traditional" CCG), and know in advance exactly which cards I'm going to get.  Since one of the rules for building a deck is that every card must be different, it is not useful to buy a second copy of any of them.

[i]Blue Moon[/i] is a well-conceived game that plays quickly, and with a lot of excitement.  It definitely scratches that CCG itch, without inflicting the pain of a true CCG.  If you're looking for that type of game experience, then give [i]Blue Moon[/i] a try.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
ConstructableCardGame, MultiOnly

A CCG-like game that is actually balanced but allows for limited deck-building (and now allows for much more expansive deck-building with the Inquisitors), and almost all decks seem equally interesting, though they fit different tastes.  A gem with a lot of replay value.
  
I keep this game around because it really does sum up a lot of CCG mechanics all in one package; the limited number of expansions keep it from being a money drain indefinitely---yet also give the game enough variety to yield a lot of replay value; the game is very, very balanced; and deck construction is really not a must, unless you truly want to, and even then it's not an all-consuming activity.

I have all the expansions, but am not about to mark each one as owned...

RATING: 5
After one play. Players build or play a pre-built deck of cards from a particular faction (Volca or Hoax) and engage one another in an abstracted war for the struggle of the Blue Moon realm. This is done by challenging your opponent to individual battles which, if won, earn you a dragon. Earn more dragons than the opponent for the win. The fun comes in building card combinations to force an opponent into quitting a fight. Also in managing your hand for future battles and knowing when to fight and when to retreat. Like all the great collectible card games, this offers player a lot of opportunity for strategic thought in composing decks and tactical thought in conducting individual battles. Also, a lot of great artwork can be found in the individual cards. They are a lot of fun to look through. There is also a lot of expandability to the system, but this is not a blind-draw money-pit: players with only the base set can play just as competively with others that own expansion material.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This two player card game seems clearly inspired by "Magic:The Gathering" with which it has many similarities. Simple basic rules but with each card having the ability to modify what is going on. Knizia's version does away with "mana" and it looks at first like a very simple card matching game. But additional cards can influence the action greatly with Knizia's version of "global enchantments" (Leader and support cards) and "creature enchantments" (booster cards). The object is to "win" engagements in such a way as to "lure" three dragons to your side in Knizia's Blue Moon universe.

The base game consists of a playing board, three nicely sculpted dragon figs (the "objects" of the game), and two decks representing two of the races in Knizia's Blue Moon universe. Decks are also available for several other races along with a couple of sets of miscellaneous additional cards. The decks come "preconstructed" and are all well balanced against each other; however, there is an option for "deck building" which can be just as satisfying as the similar process in M:tG

There is a lot of the subtlety of M:tG here without the complexity. It is very much its own game despite the superficial similarities. It is nowhere near as "rich" as M:tG but plays well and has its own charm. Best of all - it is not a CCG!!! There are the inevitable expansions, all of which appear to be well balanced; and, after an initial flurry, it appears that what is now available will be all that is required.

The theme can strike one as a bit juvenile as is the tone of the language on the cards but the game has surprising depth once you get into it. I'm happy to play it but expect it will be my grand-children that will want to play rather than my more jaded game companions...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
A hybrid of Magic the Gathering and the battle system of Hannibal: Rome vs. Carthage.

This captures the core essence of Hannibal's battles system.  In Hannibal you play cards and the opponent must match or retreat and more rounds of cards you play the greater the loss to attrition. 

Blue Moon you must match (or beat) your opponents card and when one retreats the victor gains victory points (dragons), and double victory points if the battle was six cards or more (sort of like attrition).

Since this is out of print, would be interesting if another publisher could republished as an warring ancient empires--like Rome, Carthage, Egypt and more.

Part of what I dub as the Knizia wargame trilogy--Blue Moon, Blue Moon City, Lord of The Rings:  The Confrontation.

RATING: 8.5
[u]May 2009:[/u] Just realized I still hadn't rated this one. This is a great card game. It plays easily and smoothly. There are a great deal of difficult decision making. Playing with different decks changes entrely the way you have to think. The same goes, you really have to adapt to the other decks, you just cannot play the same way against two different decks.
I might not have played enough of every confrontation to know for sure but the game really seems very well balanced.
I didn't start deck building yet and the game doesn't need that to be great. I guess I might start deck building if I ever start of becoming bored with it. But right now, without the inquisitors expansions, I don't see deck building as a great addition to this game, specially considering that, according to the rules, you'll just change 3 or 4 cards max from the standard decks.

The only reason I don't rate it higher is because of the price of it once you have all the decks, and you'll want to have all the decks, because every deck just really play sdifferently and the strategies become so much more varied.

There is a long learning curve as to play well you need to know exactly all the cards in your deck, as well as all the cards in the opponent's. This way, you can wait to have your combos come out and you can prevent the other. So you have some time before actually mastering any confrontation, however, the learning curve, even if difficultly capped, is not steep and the game is very approachable.

A word on the Vulca deck:
The Vulcas are a fire powerhorse. You want to play high cards in fire and put a lot of pressure. This doesn't mean that in earth fights, you should just quit, you still have some room to make the opponent suffer to win a dragon. It could seem as a pretty straightforward deck but it actually isn't as your win will depend on your ability to not go overkill on fire whilst giving a good fight in earth, which is feasible but not an easy task.

A word on Hoax:
The Hoax are one of my favourite decks. Their low power and tons of special texts mae them very fun to play. This is a real combo deck. It is hard to get the hang on as most often, you'll have to have the perfect timing to make its combos effective but when you do, they'll be very hard to beat. This necessary timing will make you want to know exactly what the other one is doing, even more than with other decks.

8.5 is my rating for the game overall, considering you have all decks except the inquisitors.

With just the base game, I'd rate it a 7.5 as the game is very good, lthough it won't have as much replay value.

Since for all other expansions, I'll just rate what I think of the deck, I'll rate the two base decks:

Hoax: 9
Vulca: 7

Different rates don't mean that one deck is more powerful than the other, I've already said that the decks were bamanced. This reflect more my enjoyment of playing wth this deck.

[u]October 09:[/u] Just realized that even though I've played 50+ plays of this, I still am very far from having the impression of knowing the game well. Of course this is because I've got all decks. But still, no boredom whatsoever after 50+ plays is very good!

[u]January 10:[/u] Blue Moon is back on my gaming table with a rage, it just got 20 plays in the first 10 days of january. The game is just that engrossing. You just want to play over and over again!

[u]March 10:[/u] [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/509043/multiple-player-review-blue-moon]My review[/url]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
To me, Blue Moon is a somewhat casual 2 player game. It’s not as casual as Lost Cities of course, but it’s no Summoner Wars either. It just feels relaxing when playing as the gameplay and rules are so simple (it is a Knizia game, so it’s no wonder). I like the “push back and forth” mechanism of trying to get the dragons over to your side. The base game with its two decks is neat and they feel very different to play, and the mutant is a card which can screw your opponent’s plan. I really like the support cards and how you play those along with the power cards for your character cards. The way you choose to lead a round with fire or earth, and the fact that you can always retreat and give up the round if you don’t think you’ll win it is pretty cool as is how the game can end in two ways and that there is a (albeit slight) chance to win instantly.

If I didn’t own a game like Summoner Wars I would probably buy some more factions and play Blue Moon more. My wife and a friend both like the game, but none of them love it. The same goes for me. And I don’t really see the point of owning a game which people won’t actively suggest playing, so off it went. But it is a neat game to be sure, and I actually do consider to buy the new version as you get 9 different factions…

RATING: 8
One of the greatest two players games. It is often said, that bidding games are not so good for two players. Blue Moon is the proof, that is not true!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I'm not too keen on games where decent play mandates memorization of 60 cards, but I'll make an exception here (and even forgive the lame theme).

Blue Moon is a climbing trick-taking game for two players, where each player draws from his own unique deck of cards.  In the majority of hands, both players will see every card in their deck, so it's important to know what to hold onto and what to throw away.  Much of the game involves 'flushing out' what amount to other players' trumps and aces, sacrificing one trick to win a guaranteed handful later.  The point value of a trick doubles once players become heavily invested in it, and that adds a great dimension to the questions you'll be asking yourself: Does he have this trump or ace?  Will this card be enough to flush it out, or do I have to convince him I'm in this trick for the long haul by building my bids slowly?  He's almost invested enough to double the stakes--do I keep going and actually try to win the trick, or concede now?

This is really cool stuff but you can't get to 90% of it until you know the decks pretty well.  In the meantime it's a decent, entirely tactical trick-taking game with a lot of luck.

Components: The cards are beautiful to behold and a pleasure to use. The special text is surprisingly straightforward, though the more I play it the more questions I have about how certain cards interact; the iconography is effective. I like the structured, finite, full-disclosure collectability of the game; perhaps the first “living card game”.

Experience: Much more straightforward than it looks. A few opportunities for cleverness arise, but for the most part I continue a battle if I'm able, in the hopes that my opponent won't be able to respond. The battle can turn rather quickly, based on card draws. The game is somewhat relaxing in its simplicity.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[2009-01-09 Rating: n.a. -> 9]
Bought the game for ~11€ at amazon.de

-------------------------------
Short Description
-------------------------------
Blue Moon is a card-game for two players. Each player plays with their own unique, preconstructed deck of 30 cards and tries to win a series of fights. Each deck represents one people from the Blue Moon-Universe. Included in the base-set are the Hoax and the Vulca. More people-decks are available as expensions.

In each fight, the players take alternating turns in which they normally play up to one character-card and usually one support- or booster-card from their hand. After playing the cards, the player announces their power in either earth or fire. Their power must at least be equal to the opposing players power from their last turn. The corresponding values to calculate your current power from are printed on the cards. Once one player can't at least match the announced power from their opponents turn, they have to retreat. The winning player then attracts one or two dragons, depending on the number of cards they have already in play.

When one player has attracted a fourth dragon, they win instantly. The game ends also, when one of the two players has no cards left. In this case, the player who attracted more dragons wins. In case of a tie, the player who has still cards left in his hand is the winner.

--------------------------
Comments
--------------------------
* Blue Moon is my first exposure to the card-duel-mechanism which is also used in CCG-games like Magic: The Gathering or  YU-Gi-Oh and I have to admit, that I deeply enjoy it. On your turn, you (normally) have six cards in your hand and it's your job to find a good combination of cards that will gain you enough power to match your opponent's currently announced power while staying competitive for the rest of the game.

* Although the rules are fairly easy, the game itself isn't. You have to know your deck and the available card-combinations of both your and your opponent's deck quite well in order to play effective. In this regard, Blue Moon reminds me of Race for the galaxy, where a good knowledge of cards and combinations is also the key to success. To learn the game, you can try MrKeldon's excellent AI-Version which is available at [url]http://keldon.net/bluemoon/[/url]. But be prepared to lose quite a lot in the beginning.

* While I enjoy the learning process that comes with this game, I know some players don't. So before buying the game, you should decide whether or not you have someone who will play this game with you. The somewhat limited group of players I can play the game with is the only reason, why I don't rate it higher. Would it appeal more to my non-gaming friends, it would be a sure ten.

* The game has a lot of depth to discover. Even after about 75 games (most against the AI), I learn new powerful combinations for the two people-decks of the base-set. So Blue Moon gets a thumb up for great replayability.

* The available expansion-decks seem to be greatly balanced and each one supports a different play-style which has to be discovered and learned once you get a new deck. Some of them might not fit your taste, but I guess you'll have a good time while deciding if they do. For this reason, I rate each expansion deck just like the base-game. Surely there are some expansion-decks that I like more than others, but I guess each one is a good addition to the game and enhances the replayability of an already great game.

* The game plays quick. After 20-30 Minutes you are done with it. Normally this leads to a series of games.

* Blue Moon is pure player-interaction with a high screw- and, since it is a card-game, also a built-in luck-factor. Stay away from the game if you don't like this.

* I discovered Blue Moon too late. Unfortunately it is out of print. While the base-set still seems to be widely available, the expansion decks aren't. This means, you either have to pay quite a lot for them or you can't even buy them anymore, which is a shame since I'd love to own them all.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
A card/battle game where each player takes a themed deck and fights a series of "fights" against their opponent.  A fight is simply trying to equal or better your opponent's last play.  Special powers on the cards make things interesting and lead to some interesting and suprising combinations.  Winner of a fight gets to lure dragons to their side, which is how victory is judged at the end of the battle.  The different decks will ensure this game stays fresh for literally years to come.  A wonderful game, where having a "feel" for the cards is essential - stay and fight, or retreat and come back swinging.  The "six cards played doubles the stakes" rule is inspired.  A slow burner for me, but have been playing it regularly lately, and am starting to see it's genius.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
There are a lot of good points to Blue Moon: non-collectability and gorgeous oversized cards being two key ones for me. One of the best two-player card games designs out there, and it is helped greatly by the attractive pre-constructed format. Buy as little or as much as you want without worries of collectability. It scratches the CCG itch and is better than most every CCG on the market actually.
 
Kosmos and/or Knizia must have put this through really really exhaustive playtesting because no cracks have shown in this game yet.

RATING: 6
My rating for Blue Moon is for the system as a whole rather than what comes in this box alone.  The reason I say this is that I feel that there could have been better people deck choices for a little more even match up in the base game.  Maybe that's my inexperience speaking though.  Blue Moon is great if you invest in Blue Moon.  I say that because the more Blue Moon you buy, the more variety you get in the end.  Thankfully it's not as much of a money pit as CCG's or even LCG's.  Though it is similar to LCG's if Knizia had continued releasing more decks.  If you purchase it all, you get a great variety of match ups using just the pre-constructed decks as is or alternatively you can delve into the realm of deck construction.  It somewhat scratches a CCG itch (moreso than Dominion) and for less of a price (though not as cheap as Dominion).  Definitely a good experience for the cost if you're willing to invest.  I can only see ratings going up with more plays.

RATING: 8.5
Highly rated for good reason, much like a CCG but without the collectible part.  Game-play is simpler than MtG, but initial impressions are positive.  The decks are very well balanced, and enjoyment of the game increases as you get familiar with all the cards and can plan combinations and anticipate counters.  Much of the game is about careful card management, since you usually will play virtually all 30 different cards of your deck.  The theme is somewhat unappealing and the artwork on some Vulca and Mimix cards is unfortunately somewhat risque.  Those who have similar issues and enjoy the gameplay will want to consider getting one of the expansion decks to replace the Vulca cards and for more replay value.

I also own five of the expansion decks: [gameid=19740] (earth - simpler power deck) is a good choice to replace the base Vulca (fire - power deck) against the base Hoax (scholars - trick deck).  Note that Mimix has even more risque artwork than Vulca.  Recommended as other good first choice expansions are [gameid=19736] (birds - combo deck) and [gameid=19737](children - combo deck), then [gameid=19741] (caterpillars - trick deck) and [gameid=19738] (water - speed deck).

RATING: 6
An non-collectable CCG, this is a simple 2 player contest fighting over dragons. Play characters to your side, trying to over power your opponent. Add leadership,support and booster cards to your side, engage special rules effects, and figure out what is happening. Not bad when you get the hang of the turn order, but I lost badly in the end with a hand full of low strength characters and nothing else. Because you are drawing blind from your draw deck, if you don't have the right cards in your hand, you're stuffed. The rules effects were good, but needed a little figuring, typical for this style of game. If you like CCGs, you might find this too light. If you dislike rules lawyering, this is not too bad. If you dislike direct conflict, well this is a fight game. Me, I enjoyed it but wasn't thrilled. Not quite my cup of tea. More plays will help, but fundamentally this is not my kind of game. But I do recommend Blue Moon City, which uses the same art and design, the same game elements, but is a very interesting boardgame with no rules effects to argue over.

RATING: 9
Update:  This game has risen quite a bit for me lately.  It's one of those games that I really had to play a bunch to to enjoy.  What after a couple of plays felt random has become really good now that the decks have started to sink in.  I bet it took about 20 plays with the same deck for me to really appreciate this game.  Add in all the other decks and the system has a ton of replay, which gets more tense as you know the decks better.  When I realized it's a game about timing retreats rather than blowing away opponents every battle, it got better.  Still, if you're only going to give it a couple of plays, I'd rate it a 6.

RATING: 10
Great 2 player card game that plays quickly and still has a good amount of depth. I'm bumping this up to a 10 now after about 40 plays. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Reiner Knizia's Blue Moon, aka "Magic for Dummies". Looks great, feels like a CCG, but is clearly inferior to a good CCG (i.e., MtG - howl if you want, critics, but it's undeniable). The secret lies in the ability to tune your deck to what you're expecting to play against. The fun lies in the metagame - what deck you're playing and what deck your opponent is playing. The card universe of Blue Moon is too small to make it interesting. This is a decent entry-level game for people who've never been into MtG, L5R, OTE or the other top-flight CCGs (sort of a simpler take on the old MtG entry-level variant Portal). For those who are CCG vets, it's like drinking a good table wine after savoring a bottle of Chateau Petrus... By the way, this thing is horrendously overproduced. The board and the dragons are wholly unnecessary, and the tarot-sized cards won't fit into any deck protector that I know of. The art is no better or worse than average MtG work. Kosmos was clearly looking for a few extra bucks here, but at the cost of portability. The whole game could have fit in an Adlung-sized package. A point off for that - card games like this are supposed to be portable. That said, if you want to have a simple 2P card game with the basic flavor of the old, original MtG ruleset without the baggage that the whole MtG name carries these days (unjustly, I might add) then give BM a try. MtG fans won't find anything here that they haven't already seen, and done much better in MtG. I wonder if Knizia even broke a sweat putting this game together; he should send Richard Garfield a thank-you note, if not a % of the royalties. :) *** UPDATE: After going 0-for-6 in trying to get interest from other players by teaching them BM, I have to label the game a disappointment. I'm done with BM with four boosters in shrink.

RATING: 6
I like this game. I would describe it as a variant on the card classic - war, but you hold a hand and draw cards at random rather than just a random draw. The mechs are simple and there are enough cards in a deck to keep it interesting. Plus there is a deck builder mech if you are inclined to collect decks. The artwork on the cards and the cards themselves are first rate so no complaints there. I even give high marks on theme. There definitely is a strong theme built around the mechs, problem is the theme is kinda... meh. Unlike a LotR themed game there is no popular hook. I visited the FF site to see if they provided more fluff, there was a little, but it wasn't inspiring. Lastly, come on *another* nerdy sci-fantasy setting!?! This game will chase women from the room screaming.

I would have preferred the same mechs and great materials of construction grafted on to a less ubiquitous fight night theme. Imagine Ali vs Frasier... or Chuck Norris' Kick Boxer... how about Monday Night Football!?! Any of those would have been better.

RATING: 9.5

RATING: 9
Knizia takes a stab at CCG's, and the results are solid gold.  This game is incredibly well-balanced.  Some decks are easier for beginners than others, but no deck is better than another.

The game is like a combination of tennis, poker, and Magic the Gathering.  When you play creatures, you are basically bidding, and your opponent must match you or up the ante.  But when someone gets to 6 cards, the battle is worth a lot more so if you think you don't have what it takes to win, you might want to cut your losses early.

It reminds me of tennis because the game is played in several, short rounds, and when you win a battle you capture dragons, which can be recaptured from you.  This leads to a sort of match-point scenario.  Pretty awesome idea!  And there are enough different decks and different expansions to give the game endless replay value.  One of the better games I've played.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
I have plated several dozen games against Mr.Keldons program which includes all the expansions. (I only log face to face games).

This is War turned into a real game.  It adds the choice of two domains, variable values for the cards depending on domain and special powers on some of the cards. The cards do impart a different flavor to each of the factions and there are a variety of strategies. However, there is little thematic carry through - typical of Knizia cards games. I suspect I would like the game a lot better if it was more than two player and involved four or more possible domains. As it is it strikes me as rather flat.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Do you want to know a game that is greater than the sum of its parts? Blue Moon is that game. The rules are almost too simple to ever believe this game is more than what it, in fact, is: a number comparison game, with the player who withdraws from the battle first losing a point to their opponent. But what you don't realize until you play is that the tension is HUGE and the push-your-luck aspect never feels random. The special powers are often neat and the asymmetrical balance of the different races is always intriguing. This is obviously a Knizia game (his ability to make deep games with a simple number comparison system is his greatest strength) but has a very nice Fantasy wallpaper to the whole thing. I'm telling you: get this game if you like Knizia. This is a beautiful system of his.

The fact that each deck is what it is, and the uniqueness of each faction providing new flavour Blue Moon shines.

RATING: 8
From reading the rules, the game looks like it wouldn't work at all. It sounds trite, almost pointless, like Knizia has attempted to capture the essence of a collectible card game and missed the point entirely. Knizia has fooled me before with this same trick. Ever read the rules to Flinke Pinke? How about Quo Vadis? Even Modern Art sounds kind of ridiculous based on the rules alone. Well, Blue Moon is good. Very good. I don’t yet have a sense for whether it will remain very good for a long, long time, or whether it will burn out after the decks become too familiar. It probably will burn out eventually, but I think there’s plenty of play before that happens. I’m not interested in the deck-building portion of the game; my rating is based on the constructed decks only.

RATING: 10
Past the forty-play mark now. I've played all of the expansion decks at least once. It doesn't seem like there ought to be so much fun, drama and tension in this game, but there is. With only 30 cards you're managing your deck as you pass through it, trying to keep the right amount of flow while getting the most bang out of every card. Fights can escalate completely out of control with tight spots on both sides...whew! Lots of fun, though please note that players will get the most out of the game when they become familiar with the decks; if you're only going to play it once, don't bother. I like all the expansion decks, but the Aqua and the Mimix are particularly good fits with my play style. Incidentally, my rating is that of the entire game with all the expansions; just the base set on its own would be a 7 or an 8.

UPDATE: I finally bumped this one up to a 10.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Reiner Knizia's  take on Magic -- and boy does he ever take something that is wild and crazy into something that is far more balanced AND doesn't require the ongoing purchase of further cards to play. Blue Moon is likely to remain my favorite Knizia and for good reason. It's simple enough to introduce to people but it is difficult to master. Unfortunately, any degree of mastery first comes with getting a handle of the deck you are using, but then with knowing opponents decks. This is not to say that you have to know them inside and out, but there are certainly key cards in each deck that are worth keeping track of (e.g., Flit has three birds with a value of 4. If you can force them out and into the discard pile, you put them in a bit of a tighter pickle). While some argue that there are clear 'tiers' for decks, every deck has a fair chance against every other. In short, it's just a great dueling card game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A semi-collectable Knizia card game with a great fantasy theme. It reminds me of both Lost Cities and Magic. It doesn't get a higher rating because of the inherent rules complications that arise from having so many special rules.

RATING: 6
When compared to other CCG style games such as Magic this game pales in comparison with a relative lack of strategic play style options.  However, when compared to other light euros such as the other games in the Kosmos 2 player family, this game fits right in and is a bit above average.  The fantasy style art is average at best.  Most annoying of all is the choice of components.  I hate the fact that many euros use non-standard card sizes.  The small cards in many euros are annoying, but often forgivable because the cards are usually only a small part of the game.  However, ANY game which focuses primarily on card play including BLUE MOON and Ticket to Ride should most definitely stick with standard sized cards.  They are what we are all used to holding comfortably and can be protected from wear by sleeves if heavily played.   The use of oversized cards cost this game a half-point in my rating.

RATING: 6.5
2015-10-29

Initial Rating: 6.5 (October 2015)

As most games from Reiner Knizia fell flat for me, I wasn’t in a hurry to try Blue Moon, but I was pleasantly surprised. I liked the game and I want to try it again, perhaps it can even go up in my personal ratings.

The game rules are easy to teach, but as it allow for some deckbuilding it is very interesting. I’m still not sure about how the deckbuilding is done, but it seems similar to Android: Netrunner´s. I will read about it soon, for now I have only played with the pre constructed decks.

The gameplay offers interesting decisions forcing you to choose the element of the fight, the characters and supports. It seems very simple but I like it and I’m pretty sure it has lots of hidden depth (which I would love to explore). 

The art is great and I love the Tarot sized cards, the only issue is that sleeve them is much more expensive.

I bought most of the old sets in an auction and later that week FFG announced a reprint for the game (which I also bought). I’m still not sure about the differences of the editions or if it is worth to keep both copies of the game but I will find out soon. As I bought a lot of cards at the same time, it was hell to verify if the sets were complete. Now I know how to do it, but at that time it seemed very hard.

Bottom line, I’m mystified and intrigued by the game. I really want to play it again soon and I’m pretty sure is rating will improve with more plays. I think it is a good two player game but I need more plays to verify it. 

Current Rating: 6.5

RATING: 8
This game grows on you the more you play. It's a great feel of a CCG (collectible card game) and saves you money in the long run.

I've been enjoying it and look forward to playing it more now that I'm introducing more players to it.

My record at losing when I teach is still intact! :)

This is a game that rewards multiple plays. You'll need to learn your cards and then, like many Knizia games, it starts to open up and you see combos and interactions.

Each deck has a different style of play and over all, I really just enjoy it. Part hand management, part "no guts, no glory", part push your luck.

Quick play and it gets better each time I play.

RATING: 5
This is the first of Kosmos' 2-player line of games that really did not "grab" me... and that includes Crocodile Pool Party!

The two play decks included in the basic game (Hoax and Vulca) are not very balanced... I think that the Hoax have won only 3 of the games I've played.  So guess what... I have to pump more money into the game to make it playable.

People are saying that the 'deck building' aspect is where all the fun is... which is what I was trying to avoid!  The stand-alone decks do not appear to be very well balanced, so you almost have to play with customised decks... and the 60 cards included in the basic set are definitely NOT enough.

I like the game system.  I like the way the game flows and there are some strategies that you can employ with even the basic decks.  But, couldn't they have balanced the decks a little bit?  Or made them larger?  30 cards doesn't seem to be enough.  And the Hoax lose 80 % of the time... not fun at all.

It would have been better if they put all 330 cards in one box... made it a "constructable" game and left it at that!

A pathetic attempt to cash in on the CCG market without the collectibility.  I expected more from Reiner Knizia.

I should have passed.

Pseudo-M:tG fighting (bidding) 2-player tactical card game of hand management w/o the CCG baggage.  Pleasantly impressed with my first few games as BM plays much better than the instructions read.  Familiarity with the card text of your race/deck as well as your opponents is a must as this game has much more depth than its' initial impression (though unfortunately there's nothing really new here for the experienced M:tG player).  The board and dragons are not necessary, making each stand-alone deck of cards entirely portable as is.

Expansions owned:  All to date.

RATING: 9
My favorite 2-player game once you've got all the different races.  Loads of replay and the different decks each have their own unique flavor.  Can't get enough!  While I did get all the decks, I'm doubtful I'll ever get into deck building as I simply don't think the game needs it. 

Vulca- Another pretty straightforward power deck like the Terrah, but for some reason infinitely more fun to play.  Vulca don't seem to like the game to drag on and prefer to burn their opponents down pretty quickly.  Complete with some major support cards, you come out with a pretty decent deck and a great race for players starting out.  

Hoax- As their name implies, these guys are all about "tricksies" as Smeagol would put it.  Easily one of my favorite decks as they have probably the best special text of any of the natural decks and an unrivaled dominance in support options.  For as old and wrinkly as these guys look, they're loaded for bear.

RATING: 8
An entertaining, sometimes intense and sometimes frustrating game of dueling. Artwork is great on the two base decks, the gameplay is smooth for the most part, and you really feel like you've done something when you've won (especially with the Hoax versus the Vulca). The base-set matchup is a little uneven, at least for relative beginners, as the Hoax requires a little more dexterity and planning to play. Terrah vs. Hoax would probably have been a clearer straight-up bashfest, but it would probably have given the wrong impression about the game. This game is well worth the time to master, and playing well really will require mastery in the form of becoming familiar with your deck(s). See my review for more.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Blue Moon is not a terribly complicated game at its core. You have a hand of cards with values in two currencies. In each round, you play one or more of them to match an escalating power requirement, then draw new ones. Special card types and abilities provide exceptions to all of the above and can make you overspend or underspend. If you find you can't keep up using the cards you draw, you may or must drop out of the fight, which is less costly if you do it early. A tug-of-war track disguised as some plastic dragons shows who's currently ahead; you prevail by making consistent efficiency gains and/or a few lucky gambles.

The game is often compared to Magic, but it's not a comparison that is very fair nor does Blue Moon any favours. This game is more like the framework of a mathy German card game festooned with Magic-like tricks and effects. In aspects like player expression, design space, narrative flow or sheer game space, Blue Moon just can't begin to compete with Magic, and as a number exercise it can't compete with for instance Lost Cities or Schotten-Totten. I can see how people primarily interested in one side or the other might think this is a successful hybrid, but for me it's not exciting in either regard.

Selling six of the first eight decks as expansions is a bit nefarious considering they were clearly part of the original design and if you like the game you would have wanted them all.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
You can play BM in 3 forms. The boxed set alone is a good basic 2 player card game rating 6.5 for me. Good buy, but just about average.
Adding the expansions races raises it to 7, but is more a waste of money considering the number of expansions.
However this game can also be played as a very good substitute for trading card games with advanced rules and all (or at least many) expansions. If you every wanted to get a TCG, but feared that it will be a money pit BM migth be what you are looking for. Just make sure you get at least some expansions - the base game doesn't provide the TCG feeling for me.
Another excellent aspect of the game is the balance. As this is a closed gaming system all cards have been carefully balanced against each other. So you won't see any erratas or card bans or even unbalancing super cards.

RATING: 7.5
Blue Moon is a quick two player card game where each player plays a different deck in a battle for superiority. The asymmetrical nature is fun and there are interesting decisions during play to make the game fairly engaging, however without any expansions I think the game is just OK and gets old fast. The expansion decks have some intriguing twists though and having just a few of them added into the mix really adds a lot of value. Each deck has its own strengths and weakness and the way you play each deck also needs to adjust based on which deck you are playing against. With a few extra decks in the mix there is really a lot to explore and plenty of variety and replay value in this fun and dynamic game.

RATING: 7.5
[2007.Apr.12] Blue Moon (including the additional expansions) is a well-tuned card game. Although the rules can be learned in a relatively short timeframe (~20-30 minutes), actually mastering the game takes much longer. The "fixed deck" aspect of the game is a plus--no deck construction necessary. (Note, you may tweak you own deck if you own additional expansions--but this is not necessary.) The fixed decks are well balanced and play well against one another. Each deck's flavor is quite different, allowing for various strategies and playing styles. However, in order to play Blue Moon well, you have to spend some time learning the capabilities of each fixed deck (in the basic boxed set, there are 2 different decks). Nevertheless, the basic boxed set is a bargain for the hours of play you get from it. {8}

RATING: 7
[2 plays, base set + Mimix]

Relatively light, enjoyable "war" game, but with variable player powers, a hand to choose from, and combos.  Maybe I'll start seeing more depth in this game after more than 1 play.

It is nice to have 30 different cards to choose from: each one of them has a kind of individuality that makes it all the more precious.

I also enjoyed benefiting from the occasional twist of fate that saves an otherwise desperate situation: it feels good to have luck on one's side.  Of course, the same applies to your opponent, so the luck factor is smeared over a few fights.

As regards to the obvious comparison with its older cousin Scarab Lords, I'd say that the two games play quite differently, despite their common reliance on variable player powers:

- In Scarab Lords, you progressively conquer or lose different areas of society (economic power, etc.), that each bring a specific kind of reward; the areas where you dominate slowly change during the game, which brings more tension than in Blue Moon ("I've got to get the religious power back in lower Hekumet").  In Blue Moon, the game play is made of a succession of fights, with little variations in the goal of the fight (usually: "I must win this fight").  In Scarab Lords, your strategy generally changes during a single game, which I appreciate.

- It is also quite frustrating, in Blue Moon, to spend 15 minutes playing and reach a state where all three dragons are back in the neutral zone; in contrast, the area of domination, in Scarab Lords, generally belong to one of the players: this gives a greater sense of achievement.

RATING: 9
We got this in a trade and snagged several of the expansion decks as well (Mimix, Flit, Khind, Terrah, and Bukah Invasion).  Blue Moon has worked very well so far---we really enjoy the duel aspect.  At first glance, it can look like an overproduced variant of War, but on deeper inspection, the game involves a lot of hand management.  It often feels like a tennis match where you have to try and hold your serve for each point.    For such simple rules, each deck plays differently and thematically and you have to learn how the different cards interact---once you start to figure it out, it feels very satisfying.  I also appreciate the theme and that it's more than another Tolkien/D&D clone (somewhat surprisingly, my wife even enjoys it and gets a kick out of the Khind names and artwork, her favorite deck so far).  

We played this over again when we first got it, to the point where we've probably overplayed it and my wife is burned out on it.  Hopefully after letting it rest for a little, we can bring it back out again.

Blue Moon was a game that offers the same kind of strategic decisions that occur in Magic: The Gathering. The gameplay is quite different, but it also consists of a duel between two players. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Fantastic NON-Colectible card game. Tons of strategy under what had appeared at first glance to be a stripped down exterior.

All the good stuff I liked about ccgs, without almost any of the stuff I didn't. Add to that fantastic balancing, high production values, and wonderful art direction. 

Some of the names are a bit unpronouncable and some of the others are groan inducingly comical as well as down right awful. Though if that's the game's only shortcoming, I see no shortcomings.

 While I also wish I could find card sleeves for the oversized cards, I wouldn't wish the cards to be smaller just to accomodate
being able to protect them. 

The Vulca and Mimix are wonderful decks, though it is not necessary to buy the base set, as all other decks can work independantly, given you already know the rules and can produce 3 proxies for the dragons.

It is worth it to buy all the decks, as you can then play the "Consolidated" versions fo each deck, by returning the scattered cards of other races from the base deck they are in, over to the race deck the "belong" in.

Deckbuilding with the Emissaries and Inquisitors packs should be something very fun when I get around to it.

I highly recommend this game to anyone.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Blue Moon appeals to the CCG-loving part of me, as well as to the I-can't-afford-to-spend-$1000-on-a-CCG part of me (sidenote:  I can't afford $1000 on a CCG because I've spent WAY more than that on HeroScape).  Excellent dueling card game.  The expansions and the option to customize your deck keep the game fresh.  

If you're just starting out, I would recommend the starter set plus 2 other peoples, to try things out.  I like the Aqua and the Khind would be great decks to pick up.  The Aqua are a beautifully balanced deck with some nice protected cards and free cards.  The Khind are fun because they play so differently than the others, what with their gangs.  But any 2 of the other 6 peoples would add to your gameplay. (You'll probably end up getting all the expansions in the end!)  

The Emissaries & Inquisitors are an excellent addition, particularly if you're considering building your own decks.

[i]*Own two sets each of the base game and expansions.[/i]

RATING: 7
2p, 30m.  One of the guys got the base game, and I liked playing it so much I bought one of the expansion decks: The Terrah.
This game is fairly simple on the surface, but the card interactions and tactical choices can be fun challenges.
And not just interactions within your own deck, but also with your opponent's.  The "5 crystal" tournament-style scoring actually is good to encourage you to play beyond one or two hands, which helps you to discover effective countermeasures, and correct perceived imbalances with alternative tactical plans.  For some reason I think of it as a lighter San Juan.  Everything with card interaction is like San Juan to me, which is silly.  Maybe for others MtG is the standard.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Dueling card game of unparalelled simplicity and depth: a masterpiece of game design. Decepively simple this game is all but impossible to describe in a way that doesn't make it sound underwhelming, yet it is one of the rare speciments where design, function and intent comes together in radient harmony. Perhaps Knizia's best design. This even goes through the components, with a minimal game board, which is more a player aid, and oversized cards with a surprising lack of information, which makes them pleasant to handle, a joy to behold, and instant to overview. 

**So be warned, this description will make this gem seem simple where it actually is exactly as complex as it needs be for enormous depth and richness!**

Each player choose a faction, one player starts a fight selecting either the element "fire" or "earth", of which every card has varying strengths in, and plays one or a combination of cards, which the opponent has to match or surpass or retreat from the battle. If he matches, then the original player must now in turn overcome, replacing some or all of his previous cards, or retreat. The winning player attracts one of three victory markers from the board or the opponent. When all three and an additional one are attracted to one player he wins. If one player has no more cards and must retreat the player with most victory point marker wins. That's it. 

Glorious artwork, wonderful design, great flow, outstanding design. It is a bloody shame FFG discountinued this sublime game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
First things first, now that [boardgame=147154]Blue Moon Legends[/boardgame] is out, there's little reason to consider this, unless you really like the tarot format or are a collector.

My rating is based on playing the Vulca and Hoax decks from Blue Moon Legends. The Vulca deck is excellent for beginners, but I can see how they would become quickly dull for more experienced players. While it's a competitive deck, it's not that tough to play. In contrast, the Hoax take a little getting used to but ultimately hold up very well. Played right, they'll prepare you for anything. They seem especially potent with the Buka and Hyla Emissaries. I played these guys nearly twenty times in a row, gradually getting better, and still am not sick of them. They present a challenge every time.

RATING: 6
I like fantasy themes, but the fantasy theme in this game doesn't grip me.  Artwork is good quality, though.

The gameplay is nice enough.  There are some meaningful decisions.  You have to work with the luck of the draw and conserve resources and make your opponent waste his.

The pre-built decks aren't all that balanced, but the construction rules allow you to make custom decks.  Every race has a viable custom deck, so there is depth to the strategy in the game.

Overall it's just kinda okay.  I rated it low because I don't really have fun playing it.  I don't get to make a goblin deck full of explosions.  No matter how extreme I make a deck the same basic strategy applies.

RATING: 9
Достоинства:
1. Красивая. 2. Реграбельность огромная. 3. Глубокая.
Недостатки:
1. Абстрактная: так называемый "бой" - это попытка выложить в свой ход карты на равную или большую сумму очков, чем оппонент. Кто не может поддержать планку - проигрывает.
2. Нет ощущения прогресса, т.к. после очередного боя все карты со стола уходят в сброс. Хотя, стратегичность с таким подходом всё же имеется: например, необходимо думать, какие карты попридержать для следующих боёв. Иногда, стратегически верным решением будет специально слить бой, чтобы начать с чистого листа мочить оппонента.

RATING: 6.5
Two player card game by Knizia: With a 30 card deck, each turn is part of a fight, where you play leaders, characters, boosters, supporters and mutants. Winner of a fight attracts a dragon to their side (or puts the opponent's dragon back to the middle). Winner is the person with 4 dragons or runs the opponents out of cards. Cards have special abilities, much like Magic: the Gathering. Seems to be more fun than Scarab Lords, but only playing the basic decks (Hoax vs Vulca), I'm only lukewarm on the game. For basically two decks of cards, and some rules that aren't written particularly well, I don't think you get a lot of value for your money.

RATING: 10
Rating is based on the entire Blue Moon system and not just this base set.  The rating for the base set alone is 7.

The primary skills in this game are 1) staying flexible, 2) knowing when to retreat and 3) knowing how to time the endgame.  One of the more interesting things is that how these skills are used will vary depending not only on what deck you are playing but also what deck you are playing against.

The addition of the Emissaries and Inquisitors deck adds games within the game.  Not only are you in a competition to have dragons on your side at the end, but you are also playing sub-games of when to play Influence and Interference cards.  If my rating weren't already a 10, adding these cards to the mix would add a full point to my rating.

RATING: 5
As I'm a card-gamer and fan of the fantasy genre in general, I can't help but love this game.  In short, it's a Magic the Gathering that I can collect.

Update: 
Unfortunately, I don't get to consider it often since it is a 2-player game.

But when the chance arises, I immediately think about its limiting decks that tend to play better by themselves, with a definite focus and style.  So if I play Mimix vs Khind, I'd know exactly how each side would play, and I'd know that mixing either of them with anything else would dilute their individual effectiveness (since their unique abilities rely on playing more of their own cards). 

The official way of mixing them leads to deck-building and moon-counting (each card is worth so many moons) and I'd rather play something else that go through all that time and trouble.

I'm keeping Blue Moon because I simply love some of their art, but I got better 2-player games and I just don't see myself playing it often.  

Maybe once in a Blue Moon...heh.

Update 1:  It feels like this game has all the elements to be a great 2-player card game, but in the execution, it drags more than it thrills.  I think it is because you play till the deck runs out.  Sure, you can win the game by getting three dragons on your side, but that's difficult to do, because it usually becomes a tit-for-tat, I get a dragon, I lose a dragon, type of affair.

Pity.

RATING: 9
This one has really clicked now. An impressively well-balanced game and a must with the extra six races. After the first few plays, it's natural, surprisingly intense, and - thanks to the rich theme (yes, Knizia does do it sometimes) and whimsical characterisation - you actually find yourself getting emotionally involved with your cards. Scary.

Without a doubt, the best card art of any game out there, full stop. With eight different contributing artists, it's a rich, flavourful and immersive experience.

For the sake of reference and comparison with the other decks, I rate the Vulca as a disappointing 7 and the Hoax as a solid 8.

I was really heartbroken to give up my Blue Moon collection on trade, but I received an offer that I couldn't turn down.

[i]Traded with all expansions for Innovation, Hamburgum and Alea Iacta Est[/i]

RATING: N/A
This game really captures my imagination. I haven't rated it yet because I've been playing me vs. me so far. I mostly play it by myself since I'm having trouble getting other folks into it. In order to get the most out of the game, you must play several games with the same people sets and really get to know the cards. Ideally you would play once with one people, then switch and play with the other people, and then do this several times. It just isn't a game you can fully appreciate until you've played quite a few games. You also need to enjoy complex rule-interpretation situations. At first this can be daunting, but once you work through a few sticky situations you get the hang of it. The FAQ is also indispensable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
The combination of depth, complexity and art creates a nice little world.  The [i]Blue Moon world[/i].  Whoo-hooo-hooo (fade-in theremin soundtrack).  I adore Blue Moon and its wonderfully weird peoples.  

It took me a while to get to this level of appreciation.  The ruleset is simple, but with many special situations and puzzling card powers. I kept going back to the rulebook, even after multiple sessions.  It was worth it. Not being a Magic player, I was not used to the dueling-deck format, and it took me a while to see the point. 

The deck you choose gives you strategic direction, and the cards you draw give you tactical opportunities.  This interplay of strategy and tactics is what makes the game far deeper and more re-playable than you would expect. Many games come down to a hair-finish endgame, decided by who has the better final hand, or a few more cards—obviously something to try to plan for. 

The ludicrous fantasy theme and half naked babes give you.. fantasy and half naked babes!  Enjoy the b-movie experience.

If you think Blue Moon is a matter of luck (this was my initial perception), download and play against the AI:
http://mry.fidisk.fi/bluemoon/ for mac, http://keldon.net/bluemoon/ for PC. It will teach you a lesson in hand management.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Light 2-player card game that captures the feel of a CCG pretty well.  Unlike many CCGs, drawing lots of cards is a double-edged sword, as a very important tie-breaker is how many cards you have remaining.

RATING: 8.72
Fantastic 2 player card game, with quite a lot of the feel of a CCG at only a fraction of the cost. Is perfectly playable by itself, or can be expanded with several pre-built decks representing additional peoples - some of which come with additional variants & optional rules.

There are rules for deck-building, although the original decks are fairly well-balanced.

WARNING: Although the artwork is awesome, the oversized cards can be annoying - and were previously impossible to find sleeves for if you play a lot & want to avoid wearing them out. But now FFG produce 'Tarot'-size sleeves which are a perfect fit, thanks! There is also a new complete edition due for release which supposedly has more standard-size cards.

OWN: Complete set.

RATING: 6
I'm not a fan of the CCG genre not only because of the marketing but also the knowledge of card effects to play well and the downtime involved in play reading and learning; neither am I into exploring fantasy worlds (I prefer the real world). But this is a Knizia design (my favourite designer) and it is highly regarded, so I had to give it a go. One play in, already there was a growing realisation of the thematic strength of the Vulca in the fire element. This seemingly biased problem in the game intrigued me as to how deal with it in the next game, and the fact there are only 30 cards in an Alien race to consider,this geek approach should be limited. Also this is a rare Euro game in which the game play is more involved then end of game scoring, always a plus for me. What is a nice touch is that you get a brief background to the Blue Moon mythology instead of it being forced onto you, and you learn more as you examine the alien cards text. The second game was quick, making it good candidate for lunchtime sessions with further exploration. However even with 30 cards the distribution is too detailed to be offputting for me to play with loved ones. Maybe the Blue Moon City game may make me revisit this card game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Update - When I first played Blue Moon, I had been coming off MtG and other CCGs. This was just so much less. Now, years later (and many years from playing CCGs), I have come to appreciate the game for what it is. It is a very good game and for those who do not wish to indulge in the money pit that is a CCG, this is a good substitute.

Often the game depends too much on luck but then it is a card game. It is NOT a replacement for Magic. MtG is a much deeper and more complex game. Blue Moon is quick and easily understood. It is unique in that the cards played are removed at the end of each round versus the army builds of Magic et al. At its core, Blue Moon is based on a trick taking mechanism; the other CCG's are based on incremental hits. (I realize that Blue Moon is not supposed to be a CCG but with all of the expansions and special promo cards, the no-card-is-rare claim has fallen by the wayside.) The decks are fairly well balanced and so there is no advantage to buying all of the expansions except for the variety. However, as with any of the games in this genre (Magic, etc.) once hooked it will inevitably become a money pit. (The complete Blue Moon experience will cost $100 )

This is the best themed of all of the Knizia games. When I first encountered the game I was unimpressed. There are much better trick taking games that are far less expensive and less luck based. Knizia offers another card game system that is much closer to a CCG: the Lords series (Scarab, Minotaur Lords - and one published only in Germany). The Lords series offers an significantly tougher game with some real decisions. It is much better (and cheaper) than the Blue Moon series.

RATING: 7
Great for those of you sick of the ccg marketing scheme.  It's got all the twists and turns you want in a ccg, and the mechanics are simple to learn. Games are quick and fun.  Deck construction is somewhat constrained by the rules (and non-existant with only the base set), unlike classic ccg's where 70% of the strategy is deck construction.  But I like this about it...you can worry about playing the game, not constructing your deck, and it allows non-gamers an easy entree into the game.  The seller, though, is the artwork.  It is simply a beautiful game to look at and play (Don't downplay the eye-candy...a good game with bad artwork can turn some off...this is a good game with good artwork.) **Upgrade from 8 to 9...realize that is probably the best card game I own, especially with all the expansions.

RATING: 8
Ratings of the 8 races:
art (ranges - to +) means how I like the graphic design in general, including if cards are easy to identify, if boosters and support are 
easy to tell apart from characters.

control (-- to +++) is most important to me. It values how well a player can control his own fate by picking certain cards from a pile, drawing extra cards, winning dragons, discarding unwanted cards, defending against attacks and so on.

devious (- to ++) means how well the deck is in attacking the other player like discarding open cards or preventing him from laying out certain cards.

unique (- to ++) denotes how special that race is compared to others in terms of abilities and also "feel".

total simply adds up + and -, and translates them to a BGG rating.

(note that the E&I decks use a different rating system)


Hoax: art + , control ++ , devious o , unique o , total +++ = 8.5

Vulca: art o , control o , devious + , unique - , total o = 7.0

RATING: 7.5
A fast paced expandible card game that generates numerous comparisons to Magic: The Gathering. There is that familiar MTG "feel" when playing cards in combination, and a similarly themed fantasy world for the cards, but this is mostly a game about precarious hand management. A player wins automatically when he's ahead by 4 points; otherwise, whoever has the most points wins when someone runs out of cards. You get points ("dragons" actually) by winning fights. Each turn you either concede or continue a fight. To continue fighting, you must put up new cards that meet or beat your opponents cards. This is largely a mathematical exercise, where you're summing values, and sometimes doing a little multiplying, and comparing your result with your opponent's.

The game lacks that sort of "entrenched battle" sensation you might get from a Magic: The Gathering game, because with the exception of "support" cards, your fighters only last one turn. That is, you never add reinforcements to a battle, they're only replacements. It's a strange concept to work your mind around; why do characters "withdraw" (and that's not the same as you "retreating") and get replaced by other characters? This replacement MUST happen each time it's your turn, or you will lose the fight (that's retreating the battle), even if your active characters are already adequate to repel the attack. Because of this rapid change of cards, the game lacks the positionality of M:TG, where you could have several creature cards out there at once, fighting together, holding the line, and possible working in combination. Even if you play support cards, they'll only last for one fight (usually a few turns). Still, once you get to know your deck and the deck of your opponent, the hand management becomes a little easier.

I worry that after several more plays the game will be too easy, read: random and dull. We'll see, but I can imagine knocking a half a point or as much as a point from my rating after subsequent play. Blue Moon has some definite plus points and unique qualities to it. Fights take place either "in fire" or "in earth," and most cards have different values for fire/earth. Deciding which plane to fight on is an interesting mental exercise, as is deciding when to play one of your special cards that can change the plane mid-fight (normally the fight stays on the same plane).  The decks have interesting themes, and each seems to have its own best way to play it. The fact that it's NOT a CCG is a major plus if you're a reformed M:TG junkie like me who's happy not to spend a mint on a card game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
2-player card game that has mechanisms that resemble those from collectible card games, and has a distribution model that's halfway between CCG and expandable board game, but is just as bad as a CCG.

Blue Moon is all about duels, and it does them elegantly, Love the CCG feel and the customization. Nice 2-player filler. Still, the LCG distribution model means this game is pointless unless you have at least one rival to pit decks against. Also the distribution model rips you off, because each race deck is not complete, and you do need multiple decks if you want multiple copies of a card. You don't even get the complete race if you buy a race deck. At least CCG companies are up front about ripping you off.

RATING: 5
There's something addictive about Blue Moon! The games are fast, the system is elegant, and the decks are extremely well balanced. However, if I had to live out my days on a desert island with another person (I'd prefer a dessert island), and I could choose to either take Blue Moon or all my Magic cards, I would take Magic.

The benefits of Blue Moon are that it is easy for beginners to understand, it is very balanced, it is affordable, and it doesn't take much time. If you like Magic, but don't have time to fiddle with decks, you will *probably* enjoy Blue Moon. Further thoughts: a few more plays has seen the Blue Moon wane a bit (I know, bad pun). Granted, we are only playing with the base decks, but deck familiarity and tactical repetition are dragging the game down. Next time we want to play cards, we will probably play Magic. I still think Blue Moon is a good game, and the rules are very clean. As a system, it's rather elegantly balanced, and the see-saw action if fun.

Even further thoughts: this game is definitely worth owning, but just isn't going to see the table that often. My wife refers to it as "dumb Magic" - not as an insult, but simply as a way of explaining that it employs some similar mechanics (and is fun as a result) while managing to be a much simpler game. If you find the complexity of Magic exciting, Blue Moon can be a let-down (although in a world without Magic, I would likely acquire all the Blue Moon expansion decks and rate the game higher). Playing Blue Moon makes us want to play Magic, and in the end, I've found that the conflict resolution in Blue Moon is not as satisfying. Between well matched players, the victory seems to be a matter of luck. There is no room in the game to develop much of a different long term strategy, and so it is simple for two good players to consistently make optimal or near optimal decisions to "work the system". Winning is robbed of its excitement.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Kétszemélyes kártyajáték, amiben két faj harcol meghatározott számú kártyával. Minden körben egy-egy karakter méri össze az erejét, akiket lehet erősíteni, illetve támogatni különböző lapokkal. Egy-egy csata addig tart, míg valamelyik fél nem tud már többet emelni az adott csata előtt eldöntött tűz vagy föld értékén a lapjainak. Az egyes lapok az értékeiken kívül különböző szöveges tulajdonsággal is rendelkezhetnek. A cél a 3 sárkány begyűjtése vagy lapelfogyás esetén több sárkány birtoklása. Egy menet maximum 4-0-ra nyerhető a 3 sárkánnyal, plussz a befejezéssel. Így minimum 2 nagyobb menetből áll egy játék. Ha korábban ismerem meg biztosan jobbra értékelném, de ma már annyi kétszemélyes játék van, aminél nem igazán érzem jobbnak, hogy nehéz jól megítélni Knizia 10 éves játékát. Az alapdoboz összesen két paklit tartalmaz és igazán csak kiegészítőkkel lesz nagy az újrajátszhatósága, de még így is úgy érzem egy-egy pakli elég gyorsan kiismerhető. Sokkal kevesebb változatosság van benne, mint pl. a Netrunnerben, igaz ott jóval több lap tartozik egy-egy szereplőhöz. Nem rossz játék a Blue Moon, de nem az én stílusom, nem nyűgözött le, de nehéz belekötni is, mert teljesen rendben működik.

RATING: 5.5

There are certainly special cards, but mostly this is just a fun hand management numbers game.  Sure like any card game, if you draw a bad hand you are going to lose, but there is enough room here for superior play.  Overall I think this mostly is just biding time until you get the better card.

I had avoided this for a while for fear that it would be to simmilar to Scarab Lords (which I think is downright awful).  I'm glad that I finaly got the chance to see how different it is. That said I never have any real desire to play this, and compared to other similar games out there there isn't much of a reason to come back.

My rating includes the expansions because a game like this hardly exists without them. Without the expansions, dock a couple of points and rank it just above average for the Kosmos line.

The rulebook is great! It is colorful, clear and informative.  Thumb up.  The cards are ok but I prefer more descriptive text. 

FFG should include a small novel with Blue Moon similar to what Bambus Spieleverlag did for Bottle Imp and Dr. Jekyll & Mr. Hyde.  This should increase the fun of the game by providing more background of the Blue Moon.

Vulca is a strong Fire fighter with balanced capability with certain functions hindering your opponent.

Hoax is a balanced people with functions hindering your opponent.
