=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.8
I hate this game - but I really want to like it.

This game was able to drive me round the bend - and for this reason alone we had to sell it off.

It is a [person=2][/person] design, though heavily play tested by David Farquhar. It is a simple game of hand management with variable player powers thrown in or good measure.

Players take on the role of one of the peoples of [thing=9446][/thing] in their quest for dominance. Each people have their very own characteristics and special abilities. They are finely balanced against each other, though some decks are better against certain people, none are overpowered.

Through a series of battles, each player tries to win the support of the ruling elemental dragons of which there are three. Each battle is lead by character cards attacking the other player. Support cards can be played and stay in power throughout the entire battle, whereas booster cards are just that, they boost the current character.

Each player tries to force the other player to give by playing higher value cards and/ or combos. Sometimes you might want to forfeit in order to limit your loses. 

The game is over if any player manages to persuade all three dragons over to their side. It can go back and forth, as once a dragon has been lured to your side, it goes back to neutral ground, if the other player wins the next battle.

An alternate game ending is once players run out of cards to play.

The game is fast paced and can be played in any number of ways. We switched decks after the first game (once you have been through the entire deck).

There are many tactical considerations to make and requires a good knowledge of the inherent strength and weaknesses of each people (each deck).

Our problem is in this last bit. The game requires a commitment on the side of both players. A skilled player should win more often than the unskilled player. The effort demanded of the player is not something that we wanted to put in. It is further complicated by the fact that I have a hard time constantly shifting focus, never fully understanding what I am doing or why. The different aspects of the various decks and the need to learn and understand them in order to succeed stressed me out.

In hindsight, this might have been mitigated to some extent by sticking to the base people decks and playing them extensively in order to grasp the tactical and strategical avenues open to them.

As it were, the game left me overworked, stressed and in no way enjoying myself, rather frustrated instead and therefore it was ultimately sold off.

This leads me back to my opening statement. I can see the potential in the game and I can feel it calling me, but I also know that unless I resist I will be miserable for long periods of time. I felt no connection with the various people in the game, the theme eluded me and this further made holding my attention long enough to want to really sink my teeth into it even more difficult.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
When it have a more time, I will put the comment in English. Excuses the inconvenience. 

#----0----# 

En realidad no se por donde empezar, vengo de la CCG y este juego no se parece nada a un CCG que haya jugado. Primero, por que los jugadores tienen las “mismas” cartas y  no existe esa carta desequilibrante y que cuesta 200€, aquí por 10€ todos tenemos los mismo, todos los jugadores tienen las mismas barajas…

Blue Moon, tiene un sistema de mayorías, la forma de obtener los puntos es peculiar, y los poderes individuales de las cartas (texto que hacen que alguna regla se altere), la mecánica sencilla, al estar basado en pueblos cada uno con su propia estrategia de juego, la posibilidad de “modificar” los mazos, los pueblos que amplían al juego (espero que no sean más de 4 mazos al año, si no esto se convertiría en algo muy caro)...

Por cierto, el arte de las cartas es muy bueno, y gracias a que son cartas muy grandes, los dibujos adquieren un mayor protagonismo.

La única pega, que no existen fundas para las cartas. Ya que esta son muy grandes.

RATING: 6
Bottom line is I found Blue Moon disappointing. I was a Magic: The Gathering player from the very early days (my first decks were Beta) and I enjoyed and played the game for several years until getting fed up with the rules changes and speculators. Thus, I had high hopes that one of my favorite designers, Reiner Knizia, would have created a non-collectible game that had some of the same feel and challenge. Unfortunately, Blue Moon is rather simplistic, and I found myself bored playing - something that never happened with M:TG. Knizia's Scarab Lords and Minotaur Lords are a bit more interesting, however, and worth checking out even if Blue Moon disappoints.

RATING: 9.5
(NH)

Letter Grade: A.  With all the decks, you have nearly infinite replayability in a system that already combines variable card powers, a CCG-similar feel, thematic design, quick play, and accessibility into a great game of tug-of-war.

I love several things about CCGs when played between two well-balanced decks.  Matches are exciting and unique and short, and can be tense when both players know both decks.  But I obsess over deck-building, constantly tinkering for better balance and effeciency, and it becomes far too much of a bother.  Wanted Blue Moon to provide the advantages of theme-heavy variable-text card play without the need for obsessive deck construction for balance.  Been pleased so far with several base-set plays, and my excitement level is still high (and should remain that way as we become familiar with the Vulca and Hoax and expand into other peoples).  The cards are beautiful and the base set is a great value.  

9/11/07: Up to 8.5 from 8.  One more base-set play tonight.  I really like this game and had to resist bumping it up a full point as we still haven't explored the expansions. 

03-12-08: My initial enthusiasm continues to deepen as we dig further into the expansion decks.  No sign of slow-down on this one.  

Christmas 2008: My Blue Moon collection is now complete.  Most-played decks are still the Vulca and Hoax, but all of them are unique and cool.

[05-08-09]: Old rating: 8.5.  New rating: 9.5.  My new rating system will decrease most ratings, but my appreciation for Blue Moon keeps going up.

RATING: 5
I'm a bit concerned that once a player gets an early lead in dragons, it appears very difficult to catch up.  I see very little flip-flop in the lead.  I'm also a bit concerned that the strategy for each deck seems pretty inflexible--and that each deck only has one winning strategy.  Also, I've noticed that some cards are only useful at the beginning or middle of the game, and some are obviously intended to be useful at the end of the game.  Since there's no reshuffling of the discard deck, if you get the wrong cards at the wrong time, you can get irretrievably behind very early in the game, and know you'll never be able to catch up, yet you still have to play out the hand, which can make the game less fun.

RATING: 10
PERMANENT PLACE IN COLLECTION

UPDATE: Traded for an extra copy so we can have mirror matches. Yep, I love this game.

UPDATE: Now in the running for 'best game ever'. It's the game Magic the Gathering would be if the chrome was stripped out and it wasn't a CCG with more rules than pebbles on your average beach. Knizia is a genius for creating a game with the feel of Magic, but which has about four rules and almost endless replayability with one or two pre-built decks.

Got in London on Board maths trade with several expansions. It's a battle game with beautiful graphics, lovely big cards, simple rules and a fair amount of tactics. Plays very quick, and is very satisfying. 

You have to get a higher number on your cards than your opponent so the tactics are about which cards to play when.

RATING: N/A
The world of Blue Moon is in chaos. Its god has abandoned it, and its people are in open war against each other, while the ruling power of three elemental dragons reigns above all! In this original game designed by Reiner Knizia, each player takes control over one of the Blue Moon peoples - the creative machinations of the Mimix, the fiery Vulca, the lofty Flit, and the clever Hoax - in their quest for dominance. The Blue Moon Legends basic set provides all the material needed to play, including details on the various peoples, a game board, full-color rules, and three plastic dragon figures. Expansion packs contain additional people cards.

RATING: 7
Not a bad card game. It reminds me a lot of Magic, but with a lot of things I don't like about that game fixed, including the transient nature of most cards making it so that no combo can be too terribly broken. The main problem I have is that the main interest in the game for me is deck-building, but without having other people to play with, this part falls flat. That may sound like it's more of an issue for me personally than with the game, but there are some dead CCGs I'd rather expend effort trying to get people into, and when it comes down to it, I didn't have as much fun playing this as I did Scarab Lords (another Knizia 2-player card game), and that game doesn't require any "prep work" to make the most out of it (and has a smaller but more interesting in-game deck-tweaking component itself).

Still, I wish I'd discovered this a couple of years ago when I was trying to sell my Magic playing friends on the joys of hobby gaming. I got by without it, but this probably would've made it easier :)

RATING: 7
A solid game where you play one race (the base game comes with two races, but there are expansions). The game is a series of battles in either fire or earth. At the start of you turn, you can play a leadership card (general tricks), must play a character card, and then can either play a booster (one time help) or support (continuous help throughout the fight). The fights continue until someone runs out of cards.

RATING: 10
For a game with a (pretty) simple ruleset, there's a lot of variety in this little gem.  Games are short and very tactical.  The better player will win.  I'm glad I picked this up.  Unfortunately you need to play this multiple times to really start exploring the depth of the game; in today's environment of instant gratification a good number of people will play Blue Moon once or twice, wonder what all the fuss is about and never play it again.  Which is a shame.  If you buy Blue Moon, play it at least half a dozen times before writing it off!  I'll bet things start "clicking" with you and you'll see what I mean.

RATING: 9
I play this one with my buds often -- I only have the starter set (Vulca and Hoax), but it never ceases to amuse; we always play best out of 3; if the Hoax beat the Vulca we call that "breaking serve."  Very portable and convenient -- leave the dragons at home -- most gamers can keep track of who is ahead by at most 2 points ("dragons").  Even when we have 3 or more people, sometimes we'll still play this game -- with much kibitzing and taunting from the peanut gallery.
